LESSON 6 – Meet the Inner Dreamer for More Interesting Dreams
--------------------
<v ->The dreamer is the label that I give</v> to the part of the unconscious mind that creates and plays out our dreams. The dreamer is the part of you that directs, produces, and writes the scripts for your dreams. Although your dreamer lives in the unconscious mind, it is a conscious aspect of yourself, which can learn, evolve, and even be directly dialogued with. Neuroscience tells us, that although some dreams are just used for filing and working through the day's events as a way to update our survival mechanisms and reconsolidate memory, many of our dreams are used as mediums for psychological integration, and play a vital role in our mental healthiness. When you're in a lucid dream and you call out, "Inner child, come to me", it's the dreamer that sends the inner child from stage left. When you experienced trauma, it is the dreamer that decides to replay the traumatic event in your dreams as a way to work through the trauma and heal, and when you fall asleep asking for a lucid dream, it is the dreamer who grants your request. Make friends with your dreamer and the doors to your dream world is unlocked. So what's the best way to connect to your dreamer? By paying attention to your dreams. People often tell me that they don't write down their dreams 'cause their dreams are so boring, to which I always reply, "Your dreams are so boring "because you don't write them down." Imagine this, five times a night, your dreamer has to create original Hollywood pieces of script writing to present to your conscious mind. Now, imagine if every night of your life, you're not listening to that, you're not watching those scripts, you're not there in the theater seeing it be played out. I did a script writing degree at university, and I know if you asked me to write five unique scripts every night, and I knew there was no one in the audience to watch them or witness them, I just start writing really boring scripts. That's what happens with our dreams. Start writing down your dreams and the content of your dreams will become more meaningful. There's even a scientific study that has shown, people who ingest more complex narratives like people who go to the theater a lot, read a lot of novels, expose themselves to complex narratives, in theater, film, or storytelling, they have more complex dreams, because the dreamer learns narrative, the dreamer learns about red herring, the dreamer learns how to construct stories. So, if you're having boring dreams, you want to have some more powerful dreams, read Tolkien before bed, watch a film that's really complicated, go to the theater more, and your dreams will start to reflect those complex narratives. So that's why we have to keep doing the dream diary, yes. I know dream diaries are probably the least sexy part of lucid dreaming, but it really is a vital part of connecting with our dreamer, and trainings to have lucid dreams. But keeping a dream diary isn't the only way to connect with your dreamer. Look at how you about your dreams in everyday life. For many of us, we use words that have negatized and pathologized dreams and our everyday parlance. For example, you are a dreamer. It was just a dream. You're dreaming. We use dreams in a negative way. We live in a society that has pathologized a third of our life. So look at the language which you use to talk about your dreams, and look at your energetic connection to that third of your life that you spend sleeping and dreaming. Change the energy, and the energy of your dreams will change too. We need to start viewing our dream to something valuable. Once we start to view them as something more valuable than they are, the value they offer us will increase naturally. Once we start having lucid dreams, you're going to be able to meet your dreamer face to face. But until then, let me guide you in a meditation that will help you connect with your dreamer right now. In this guided meditation, we're going to connect with our dreamer, the part of the unconscious mind that creates and plays out our dreams. In order to connect with the dreamer, we're first going to show gratitude to ourselves, gratitude to our body, gratitude to our mind, and then gratitude to our dreamer. The reason for this is because gratitude undercuts the ego. Once we're in a state of deep gratitude towards ourselves, a direct line of communication opens up to the deepest depths of our mind. Take a moment to notice the ground beneath your feet or the connection points of your body with the ground or the bed beneath it. Take a moment to connect to your breathing. Notice how the body expands when we breathe in, and how the body releases and relaxes when we breathe out. on each exhalation, allow yourself to relax deeper and deeper into the natural state of relaxation. And then, using your breath to guide you, I want you to imagine that you breathe down into your feet and your legs, and as you follow your breath to your feet and your legs, your attention moves with it. I want you to put your attention into your feet and into your legs. Really feel into your feet and your legs. Take a moment to consider the amazing job that your feet and your legs do. They allow you to walk, to stand, to dance, to run. Your feet and your legs are amazing, but when did you last say thank you to your feet and your legs? Take a moment now in your own way, in your own mind to say thank you to your feet and your legs. And now, using your breath to guide you, bring your attention into your hands and your arms. Take a moment to really feel into your hands and your arms. Take a moment to consider the amazing job that your hands and your arms do. Your hands and your arms allow you to right, to touch, to feed yourself, to hug. Your hands and your arms are amazing, but when did you last say thank you to hands and your arms? Take a moment now to show gratitude to your hands and your arms. And now, allow your awareness to spread into the core of your body. Becoming aware of your respiration system, your digestive system, your ever beating heart. Your body is amazing, but when did you last say thank you to it? Take a moment to say thank you to your respiration system, your digestive system, your ever beating heart. Show gratitude to these parts of your body now. And now, allow your awareness to spread into the rest of your body, so that from the tips of your toes to the crown of your head, you are aware. Consider the amazing job that your body does. However broken or ill your body may seem, it is always trying its best, so take a moment to say thank you to your body now. And from our body, we move even deeper to our minds. Take a moment to become aware of your mind. Take a moment to consider the amazing job that your mind does. Creator of reality, filter of experience, the most powerful virtual reality simulator known to man, the human mind. Take a moment to say thank you to your mind now. From our body to our mind, from our mind to our dreamer. The part of the unconscious mind that creates and plays out our dreams. We say thank you to the dreamer, thank you for the nightmares that offer such guidance, thank you for the dreams of insights, thank you for the dreams of prophecy, thank you for the lucid dreams we have had or are yet to have. Take a moment to say thank you to your dreamer now. And now that we've shown gratitude to our body, to our mind, and to the dream that resides within our mind, we are in a perfect place to make a request to the dreamer. Think of a request that you would like to ask from your dreamer. Maybe you ask to remember your dreams, maybe you ask for lucid dreams, maybe you ask for dreams of insight, whatever it is, take a moment now with gratitude to make a request of your dreamer. Make your request now. And knowing that your dreamer has heard you, allow your awareness to move from the dreamer back to your mind, from your mind back to your body, and from your body back to your breath. If you're doing this practice during the day, take a moment once again to say thank you to yourself, and then open your eyes if they were closed, and bring yourself back to fully wakeful awareness. So here are your actions for today. Firstly, share with the Tribe the state of your current relationship with your dreamer. Be sure to keep reciting the dream, recall affirmation as you fall asleep, and be sure to write in your dream diaries every morning, even if you don't remember anything. It's totally fine to write that too. On the seventh day of creation, God rested. But He was the creator of time so He could afford to chill. We on the other hand, own on a 30 day quest. So although we won't have a big session tomorrow, we do still have more to explore. It's all fun, though. At the end of the week, we have a quiz. I can see the hyper competitive members of the Tribe lighting up. We have our week one Pep Talk, and we have our weekly bedtime story. See you tomorrow.

LESSON 7 – Summary of Your First Week
--------------------
<v ->Today is about fun, inspiration and relaxation.</v> The fun bit is the quiz. The inspiring bit is the pep talk and the relaxation bit is the bedtime story. So, welcome to the week one quiz. Without checking back in the previous lessons of the quest, I want you to answer the following questions from memory. There'll be no shaming if you don't get them right and this is just for fun, so enjoy. Question number one. What part of the brain is activated when we become lucid? Yeah, that's right. It's the prefrontal cortex or the right dorsolateral prefrontal cortex if you want to be a real geek. Question two. How many times should we recite the dream recall affirmation as we are falling sleep? Yeah, 21 times. Question three. What has been shown to increase the narrative complexity of dream content? You've got it. Consuming more complex narratives from reading books or watching movies. Question four. What are the two most important mental qualities required to learn lucid dreaming? Enthusiasm and determination. And our final question just for fun. Which form did my divine feminine take when I met her in the lucid dream? Damn right. Freaking Beyonce. Firstly, well done for completing week one of the quest. You just started out on a journey that may radically reshape 30 years of your life. Big respect to you from me. We worked hard this week. Nailing all the basics like a boss. We've explored the what, why and how of lucid dreaming while also learning our first three techniques, dream recall, dream diaries and dream planning. The main things to remember this week are this. You need to be reciting the dream recall affirmation every time you fall asleep and the dream diaries need to be written in every single morning, even if you don't remember anything. The last thing you see before sleep and the first thing you see when you wake up, needs to be your dream diary. So make sure you've got one that you want to use. If you're still just using scraps of paper, go and get a good dream diary that you really like. Many of you may start getting lucid straight away but for others, the first two weeks of the quest will be mainly preparing the foundations and then week three is when we really start cooking with gas. Remember, your dream plan may well be the most important technique there is because the why is more important than the how. So look back over your dream plan. Does it still make you salivate? If not make a new one. There are two routes to lucidity. The first route was simply to follow the formula. The techniques work and they will bring you to lucidity. The second route, is to have loads of enthusiasm and determination that will also get you there. But I propose a third, if we combine the step-by-step formula of effective techniques with enthusiasm and determination, then we've really got something special. We've had loads of new information this week. So before we move on, let me tell you about the three stage creative process, saturation, incubation, illumination. We've just had a week of saturation. We've saturated our brain with loads of new information. This saturation process will eventually lead to illumination in the form of a lucid dream, but only if we are sure not to miss out the middle stage, incubation. Incubation is essentially doing nothing. Giving the brain a period of rest in which the insight can arise within. Today, your incubation stage is going to be your bedstory. So relax and enjoy. Here are your actions for today. As today is a review and implementation day, it's the perfect time to catch up on any content that you've missed. So let's say you missed day four or you worked too quickly through day three, go back and watch them again. Catch up on anything you've missed, rewatch videos, make sure you're up to date so that when we move into week two, you haven't missed anything. And as always keep reciting the dream recall affirmation as you fall asleep and keep up the dream diary once you wake up. Also, make sure you know your dream plan off by heart or at least your sankalpa off by heart, so that once you're in the lucid dream you don't have to think about it. You can just roll it off the tongue. I'll see you next week when we move into week two of our lucid dreaming quest.

LESSON 7 – Meditation: Bedtime Story: “Be a Salmon”

- Get into bed, get comfy, and allow yourself to drift off to sleep. While I tell you a bedtime story, I want to tell you a story about a salmon. A salmon is a fish that swims upstream, all the other fish swim downstream, and so does the salmon at first, because going with the flow seems so logical and so normal. But one day, something awakens within the salmon, a desire, a yearning, perhaps, to return home. And so one day, one ordinary day, just like today, the salmon makes a choice, a choice to do things differently, a choice to stand out from the crowded shoal. One day the salmon decides to start swimming upstream to find its way home. You know, the thing about salmon is that their journey up river is not random. They've actually got a form of inbuilt GPS that allows them to use the magnetic field of the earth to find the exact bend on the exact part of the exact same river where they were born. As the salmon swims upstream, it passes all the other fish in the river who are all swimming the other way. The other fish laugh at the salmon saying, Hey, you are crazy. Why don't you just go with the flow? Stop swimming upstream. Forget about going home. And for a minute, the salmon questions itself and thinks, why am I doing this? Why don't I just go with the flow like everybody else? And then the salmon remembers, oh yeah, I'm making my way home. And so it ignores the other fish. It is proud of its different path, and it dedicates its energy to coming home. Two and a half thousand years ago, the Buddha described the spiritual path as going against the stream. He said that it was about turning around in the river and observing how the way everyone else is going may be the easy way, but it's not the way to freedom. It's not the way home to enter onto the spiritual path, and definitely onto the path of lucid dreaming, it's to become like a salmon. Don't go with the flow of the masses who work, eat, sleep, and repeat. Be like a salmon. Don't disregard your dreams and see sleep as wasted time. Be like a salmon. Don't ignore 30 years of your life and sleep. Walk non lucidly through the rest of it. Be like a salmon. And when the others question us saying, why do you care about dreams? Just go back to sleep. What good is lucid dreaming? Anyway, shout back at them joyfully. I am a lucid dreamer and I am my way back home. Wake up. Come join me. Come and be like a salmon. And now with the energy of that story in your body, close your eyes if they're still open. Allow yourself to release into the support of your bed and relax deeply into sleep. Allow your breathing to slow and your mind to relax deeply into sleep. Allow any tension in your body to dissolve as you exhale and relax deeply into sleep. Dream lucidly, dream deeply. Relax deeply into sleep.

Week 2: Interpreting Your Dreams

====================

LESSON 8 – Recognize Your Dream Signs
--------------------
<v ->Yes, yes dreamers, welcome to day eight,</v> and our second week of the Quest. This week is all about making friends with sleep and dreams. So we'll be learning all the science around how we sleep, the different sleep stages and how we can harness our sleep cycle to help us become lucid. But first of all, let's make friends with one of the most common features of our dreams, dream signs. If I blindfolded you and took you into a bakery, I reckon you'd still be able to tell me where you were, right? Although you couldn't see the bakery, its smells, sounds and atmosphere would be enough to indicate your whereabouts. You smelled the aromas of a bakery and experienced this atmosphere so many times, that you're able to recognize one even through a blindfold. In the same way, we can come to recognize the dream state even when blindfolded by non-lucidity. How, by getting to know its unique sights, sounds and atmosphere. This forms the basis of spotting dream signs. A dream sign is any improbable, impossible or bizarre aspect of the dream experience that can be used to indicate that we are dreaming. One of the most important reasons for keeping a dream diary is to write down, recognize and acknowledge our personal dream signs. Once you know your dream signs, you're one step closer to lucidity. There are three main types of dream sign. The first one is called anomalous. This is kind of the crazy stuff you have in dreams all the time. Talking dogs, Ninja babies, dead grandma's, crazy, anomalous, one-off dream scenarios. The second type is thematic. This is where the dream itself may not be full of Ninja babies and talking animals, but the theme of the dream is what's weird. Maybe you're dreaming you're back at school when you're an adult or you're in your childhood home when you haven't lived there for 20 years. The theme of the dream is what can indicate to you that you are dreaming. And the third type is recurring. A recurring dream sign is any dream sign that's appeared multiple times, maybe even on a weekly basis. If you've got some recurring dream signs, you have a recurring opportunity for becoming lucid. So how to dream signs work? You wake up and you write down your dreams. Then you go back through the dream, checking for dream signs. Then, by acknowledging our particular dream signs in the waking state, you naturally create a lucidity trigger, Ninja babies are my dream signs, So Ninja babies equal I'm dreaming or being back at school is one of my dream signs, so being back at school equals dreaming. Those lucidity triggers will be activated. The next time you see that dream sign in your dreams, thus triggering lucidity. Every time we recognize a dream sign in the waking state, we create a critical reflective habit of mind and it's that habit that leads to lucid dreams. So even if you don't have any recurring dream signs, don't worry because every time you take the time to recognize a dream sign, you engage the habit of critical reflection. And it is that habit that becomes activated within the dream, thus leading to lucidity. Let's do an exercise to help demonstrate how we can spot our dream signs. I want you to see how many anomalous, thematic and recurring dream signs you can spot in the following dream. Let's say I have a dream that I'm walking down the street in London with my dog, Waffles. I wake up, I write down the dream and I look for dream signs, what are they? Well, I do live in London. I do have a dog called Waffles and I do often walk down the street with her. So in this particular dream, there were no dream signs. There was nothing in the dream that could indicate that I was dreaming. Not every single dream has dream signs. Although most do if you look closely enough. Let's say for example, the next night I have another dream. In this dream, I'm walking down the street in London with my dog Waffles, and at the end of the street I see Kanye West standing next to a blue dragon. I wake up, I write down the dream, and I look to see, where are the dream signs, what are they? Well, I do live in London. I do have a dog called Waffles, and I do often walk down the street with her, but I don't know Kanye West yet. So Kanye would be an anomalous dream sign. And of course the blue dragon would be an anomalous dream sign too. Just by recognizing and acknowledging those dream signs, Kanye West and the blue dragon, I have helped to strengthen a critical reflective habit of mind. And it is that habit that flows into your dreams and helps you get lucid. Now, I want you to imagine that Kim Kardashian has that same dream. She dreams that she is walking down the street in London with Waffles the wiener dog. And at the end of the street, she sees Kanye West standing next to a blue dragon. She wakes up, writes down her dream and looks for the dream signs. Let's help Kim out here, what are her dream signs? Yeah, the first one is Waffles. She's never met Waffles, so Waffles is an anomalous dream sign for her. The next one is being in London, a city in which she does not live, so that's a thematic dream sign for her. And finally, Kanye standing next to the blue dragon. Kanye is not a dream sign for her 'cause she sees him every day in her real life. But of course the blue dragon still is an anomalous dream sign, or maybe a recurring dream sign. If she dreams are blue dragons on the regular. So you get it right? Once you pinpointed your dream signs, you make a determined effort to be on the lookout for them in the future. This effort will permeate into your dreams and eventually you'll start recognizing dream signs while you're dreaming, and that's how you become lucid. In fact, it's the most common form of lucid dream to be in a dream, you see a dream sign, go what, that's crazy. I must be dreaming. It's called a dream sign initiated lucid dream. If you've got any recurring dream signs, that's really great because that means it's a recurring opportunity to get lucid, but don't forget, simply by recognizing and acknowledging any dream sign from any dream, we strengthen this critical, reflective habit of mind, and that's the main reason we get lucid. Now you may think, well, I've been having crazy dreams full of dreams signs for years and I haven't been getting lucid. Yeah, naturally, because although your dreams have been full of dream signs, you haven't been recognizing and acknowledging them each morning, right? And so you haven't been strengthening that critical reflective attitude. Once you start doing that, then lucidity's going to start coming. There are no universal dream signs, wherever the books tell you, even the classic being naked in public dream. Well for most of us, it would be a dream sign, right? But for 3.7 million British people who described themselves as practicing nudists, their dream would be the opposite. It would be wearing clothes in public in their dreams. Oh my God, I'm fully clothed, I'm so embarrassed. 3.7 million, who knew? We seem so reserved, the queen must be appalled darling. And now your actions for today, from now on, after you write down your dreams in your dream diary, read through them again and reflect on your dream signs. Each time you recognize one, take note of the dream sign, either simply in your mind or by making a little DS next to it. So you can see dream sign, dream sign, dream sign, dream sign. Once you started doing this, I want you to share your current dream signs with the tribe. Have you got any recurring ones? What's the craziest dream sign you've ever had. Of course, continue falling asleep doing your dream recall affirmation as per usual and keep up the dream diary every morning. Recognizing dream signs is not only an important lucid dreaming practice, but it's also a really fun one because you can start to see how the frequency of your dream signs increase as you progress with your lucid dream training. In fact, some of you may find that tonight, you start having really crazy dreams full of dream signs. That's a really good indicator because it shows that your dreamer really wants you to become lucid. Send in Kanye West riding a blue dragon, that should do it. It's a good sign, so I hope that tonight, you all have dreams full of dream signs, and more importantly, that you recognize those dream signs and become lucid.

LESSON 10 – 3 Steps to Manifesting Dream Signs
--------------------
<v ->Today, we will learn a technique</v> to help us manifest our dream signs into our dreams, as well as how lucid dreaming is about making friends with ourselves. Lucid dreaming is not about dream control. As I mentioned before, the central metaphor that I like to use is from my friend, the lucid dream author, Robert Waggoner. He says, "Just as no sailor controls the sea, so too does no lucid dreamer control the dream." Think of it like this, think how arrogant a sailor would be to say, "I'm controlling the sea." No sailor controls the sea. But a good sailor respects the sea so much, has so much knowledge about the sea, is so aware of the position of the coral reef, the sea monsters and how the stars affect the tides that they can sail as if they were in control. That's the attitude we need to have when working with our lucid dreams. We don't want to dominate, force, subjugate, control the dream, we want to make friends with it 'cause if you can make friends with your dreamer, you make a very powerful ally. And for those people who do think lucid dreaming is dream control, they've simply underestimated the power of what they're dealing with. If you think of the conscious and unconscious in that iceberg model where the top 10% above the surface is conscious and the bottom 90% beneath the surface is unconscious, then to think that your itsy bitsy 10% egoic consciousness could in any way control the awesome power of the 90% unconscious mind has completely underestimated the power of what you're dealing with. So you can't control the dream anyway but you can make friends with it. The reason that I push this idea of not controlling the dream so strongly is because I was introduced to this idea very strongly myself. Before I tell you the story, I need to drop in the concept of what I call the 1%. I believe that in a lucid dream, 99% of everything in the dream is you. It's a projection of your own psychology but I also believe there is a crucial 1% made up of archetypes of the collective unconscious, blood and bone ancestors, dead relatives and also perhaps the potential of enlightened beings, dream walkers to enter our dreams. But 99% is you. But there is that crucial 1%. When I first started teaching lucid dreaming, I was 25 and I felt pretty out of my depth. When my Buddhist teacher first authorized me to teach, I came up with this notion that I had to have full control over my dreams in order to be a good Buddhist lucid dreaming teacher. Of course, the more I tried to control my dreams, the more they fought back. In one of these dreams, I'd become lucid and I looked up at the sky and I used to be able to go freeze and I could pause the dream in mid-air like that. Then I could look to the sky and make one side of the dream go black and white and the other side of the dream stay color. It was just an ego trip. It was just trying to prove to myself look at this amazing control I can have over my lucid dreams. I'm playing God here. Just a complete ego trip. Now, one of those times where I'd frozen the dream and changed the color, suddenly, this Tibetan woman walks in. She was not young but not old either. Maybe mid-60s. Long hair down to the floor. She walked up to me and went, "Don't control the dream. We don't like it." I paused and in my arrogant looked at her and said, "What do you mean we don't like it? It's my dream." And then she tapped me on the shoulder, said, "Don't control it. We don't like it." Who the hell was we? The energy that she exuded and the fact that she was the only part of the dream that could still move when I'd frozen everything else makes me believe that she was something from the 1%. Perhaps the archetype of the wise woman come to tell this arrogant 25-year-old not to control his dreams. So ever since then, I made a pact. Anytime I do a course or workshop, I always tell people don't control the dream, make friends with it. In fact, your lucid dreams have been making friends with you ever since you're a kid because children naturally have lucid dreams. Not every child every single night but a Harvard study has shown that the majority of children aged between six and 16 report lucid dreams as part of their evolutionary development. So everybody watching this quest, you probably have had a lucid dream before. In fact, you probably had dozens, you just don't remember them. But something in you does. The archetype of the inner child. And that's why in this quest, we have so many of the techniques, which are quite childlike, quite playful because if we can tap into the power of the inner child, we can tap into our lucid dreaming potential. In fact, I encourage you to talk to your kids or any kids that you might know about lucid dreaming. And you'd be surprised how many know exactly what it is and say, "Yeah, I have those dreams sometimes. Now onto another exercise. Dream sign manifestation. As we've learnt before, once you pinpointed your dream signs, make a determined effort to be on the lookout for them in the future. This effort will then permeate into your dreams and eventually you'll start recognizing dream signs while you're dreaming and become lucid. But here is a way of speeding up that process. Rather than waiting for the dream signs to show up, intentionally manifest your dream signs into your dreams. This technique aims to intentionally manifest a particular dream sign into your dream, thus triggering lucidity. Here are the three steps to do so. Step one, choose the particular dream sign that you want to manifest. If you have a recurring one, use that. If not, just use one that feels particularly strong to you. Kanye West, for example. Step two, the next time you pass through that hypnotic hypnagogic state at night, recite the dream sign manifestation affirmation. For example, tonight I dream of Kanye. When I dream of Kanye, I know I'm dreaming. Tonight I dream of Kanye. When I dream of Kanye, I know I'm dreaming. Step three, repeat step two at least seven times with enthusiasm and determination before moving on to your dream recall affirmation. By doing this, essentially you are asking the dreamer send me the dream sign, let's me dream of my dead grandma, let me dream of being naked in public, let me dream of Kanye West. Knowing that to dream of your dream signs makes is much easier to get lucid and will in many cases set off that trigger and lead to a spontaneous lucid dream. And now your actions for today. Firstly, practice the Dream Sign Manifestation exercise. As you fall asleep through the hypnotic hypnagogic, be asking for your dream signs to come into your dreams. Secondly, if you have kids, or if you know any kids, I want you to talk to them about lucid dreaming and share your findings with the Tribe. Did your kids know what lucid dreaming was? LESSON 11 – The 4 Stages of Sleep
--------------------
<v ->We sleep for a third of our lives.</v> That's about 30 years that most of us know nothing about. That's crazy, right? How can we leave the school system, in Europe at least, knowing nothing about a huge chunk of human existence? Dreamers, let's go back to school, night school. I want to take a look now at the scientific description of how we sleep. Modern day science breaks down sleep into four main stages. The hypnagogic state, light sleep, deep sleep, and dream. Let us look at each one in detail now. Stage one is called the hypnagogic state. Now this is a state we've looked at already because we've harnessed the hypnotic power of the hypnagogic state for some of our lucid dreaming techniques. But what are the qualities of the hypnagogic? In the hypnagogic you'll feel very drowsy, your eyes will be closed, the brain will go into deep Alpha and Theta, and you might start having the hypnagogic hallucinations. The little mini dreams, flashes, fades, faces, geometric patterns that enter the mind as we're drifting off to sleep. You might also have these things Do you ever get those when you're falling asleep? Myoclonic jerks. So myoclonic jerks are usually associated with a lower level of respiration, which is in turn usually associated with falling asleep quickly. Meaning that you could probably do with an extra couple of hours of sleep if you do have a lot of those jerks. The main thing is, that the hypnagogic state is the doorway into sleep. Every time you fall asleep, you have to pass through the hypnagogic. Stage two of sleep is called simply light sleep. And light sleep makes up the majority of the time we spend sleeping. It seems from the outset that not a lot happens in light sleep, but actually this is not true. In light sleep, you engage procedural memory learning. Whereas dreaming sleep is used for integration of our psychology, psychological learning, integration of trauma, working through our mind therapeutically, light sleep is used for learning procedurally. For example, if you're learning how to drive a car, it's in light sleep that your brain will be going over the steps of how to drive a car. It won't be like dreaming, it'll be more like thinking through a process. And if you wake someone from light sleep and say, what were you dreaming about? They'll often say, I wasn't really dreaming, I was kind of thinking about something. In fact, it is possible to be conscious within light sleep. Have you ever had the experience of listening to yourself snore? If you have, you are conscious listening and unconscious sleeping and snoring at the same time. Now, if that ever happens again and you're by yourself, stay in that state, listening to yourself snore because from a Buddhist point of view, you're engaging sleep meditation. But if there's someone lying next to you in bed, don't be antisocial, wake up and stop snoring. Then we have stage three. Stage three deep sleep is sometimes called Delta wave sleep because the dominant brainwave of deep sleep is Delta. If you look at the brain waves of the waking state and the dream state for that matter, they look like this. There's loads of activity, there's loads of stuff happening. But in deep sleep, your brain waves look like this. Very slow long amplitude brainwaves because your brain is almost entirely inactive. The brain never switches off completely, but sometimes it does go into standby mode. That's what happens in deep sleep. So in deep sleep, you're very unlikely to be dreaming, but the brain is doing a lot in that space. One of the first things that happens in deep sleep, is your blood capillaries start going big, small, big, small, big, small, which creates a flushing motion through the brain, which actually flushes through the cerebral fluid, helping to remove toxins from the brain. This is why if you miss a whole night's sleep, the next day you might have something called brain fog. Brain fog is the psychological manifestation of the physiological phenomenon of toxins not being flushed through the brain. Another thing that happens in deep sleep is that human growth hormone is released. It's in deep sleep that your hair grows, and your nails grow, that your muscles grow even. Let's say you've been pumping iron in the gym all day, if you don't get enough deep sleep that night, the changes to your muscles will be much, much less than if you had, because in deep sleep the human growth hormone is released. The same goes for people who are trying to diet as well. If during the day you've been reducing your calorific intake because you've been dieting, but that night you don't get enough deep sleep, you may lose weight due to the reduction in calories, but the long-term effect on your metabolism will not be engaged. So deep sleep is so important for flushing toxins through the brain, for helping our body grow, and for making changes to our body's metabolism. And then we have REM dreaming sleep, rapid eye movement dreaming sleep, so-called because the eyes start to move rapidly. The body goes into paralysis to stop you acting out your dreams, and the brain becomes highly active as it starts to create the amazing three dimensional hallucinations that are so realistic we believe they're real. Think about that for a minute, you believe your dreams are real until you wake up in the morning and go, oh, I was dreaming. That's how realistic dreams seem to the brain. The reason that we dream is still up for debate, but two things we know for sure, dreaming is about reconsolidation of memory, and about integration of trauma. If you stop somebody dreaming, their short-term memory gets skewed pretty quickly, and their ability to integrate trauma is removed too leading psychosis setting in very quickly. Dreaming is very, very important. And that's why the brain prioritizes it over other sleep stages although all stages of sleep are very important. And finally, we have the hypnopompic state. Whereas the hypnagogic state is the gateway into sleep, the hypnopompic state is the gateway out. If I wake you up during any stage of sleep, you have to pass through the hypnopompic before you wake up. Now, whereas most people are aware of the hypnagogic state, they're aware of that drowsy state as you're nodding off on the bus, or they're aware of that state as you're falling asleep, many people are not aware of the hypnopompic. And for many of them it's simply because they wake up so quickly. If you wake up with an alarm clock, you get boosted out of the dream state into the waking state without experiencing that transitional space, the hypnopompic. But have you ever woken up without an alarm clock? Maybe the bird song's woken you up, or the sound of your partner making breakfast and you stop dreaming, you wouldn't say you're still asleep, your eyes are still closed, you can feel your body in the bed? That space, that's the hypnopompic. From a Buddhist point of view, the hypnopompic state is said to be one of the most refined levels of human consciousness, and a place in which insights from our true spiritual nature can manifest spontaneously. So tomorrow morning don't wake up so quickly. Hit the snooze button, drop back into that hypnopompic space and explore the power of your own mind. When we first fall asleep at night, our journey into sleep might look something like this: we close our eyes and enter the hypnagogic. Maybe we're there for 10, 15 minutes. Then at a certain point, we black out and we enter light sleep. In the hypnagogic, we can hear sounds in the room, we can feel our body in the bed. But in light sleep, we're blacked out. We spend maybe 15, 20 minutes in light sleep. Then we drop down into deep sleep for a big chunk, 30 or 40 minutes of this deep brain cleansing sleep. Then the brain does a full 180, and goes from entirely switched off to fully switched on as we start to dream. That first dream period is short though. Only maybe like five or 10 minutes. Add all that up together and you get roughly a 90 to a 100-minute sleep cycle. That 90-minute cycle continues throughout the night. But what changes is the amount of time you spend in each stage. The first three cycles, so roughly the first four and a half hours of sleep, are mainly deep sleep with short dream periods. Then after that third cycle, after the first four and a half hours, it flips, and we start having much less deep sleep and these long extended periods of dreaming. This is why for lucid dreamers our main focus is on the second half of the night, and especially the last two hours when we go into full on long REM dreaming periods. That sleep cycle, hypnagogic, light sleep, deep sleep, dream, occurs when we first fall asleep at night. But if we were to have an afternoon nap and go to sleep in the middle of the day, we'd go straight from the hypnagogic into dream, direct access. So that means that napping is really good for lucid dreaming. So please, while you're on this quest, nap as much as you can, it might be in your daytime that you have some of your most powerful lucid dreams. While you can have lucid dreams in the first few hours of your sleep cycle, the dream periods will be short and your mind might still be quite groggy 'cause you haven't had much sleep yet. However, in the last few hours, you'll not only have longer dream periods, but you'll also have a fair few hours of sleep under your belt. So your mind will feel fresh and more ready to engage lucidity. Although the majority of people may sleep in the way we just described, you may not be part of that majority. So get to know how you sleep, not how everybody else sleeps. The main thing to remember is this, the first half of the night is mainly deep sleep with short periods of dream, the second half is mainly dreaming without much deep sleep. And now for your actions for today, I want you to see how many sleep stages you can be aware of tonight. For example, can you notice the hypnopompic state as you wake up in the morning or in the middle of the night? Can you listen to yourself snoring while being aware of light sleep? And of course, can you be aware of REM dreaming sleep and become lucid? I'd like you to share with the tribe, how many sleep stages you are able to be aware of? And of course, keep up the 3D's and the dream sign manifestation technique. We're going to have loads more lucid dreaming techniques coming up, but for now we need to keep strengthening the foundation of those habits. Also, don't forget to check in with your tribe dream circles. So I hope that filled the educational gap that school left behind, and that simply by being aware of how sleep works, you're not only better equipped to know when to focus your lucid dream training, but also better equipped to make the most out of every stage of sleep because each one is vital to our health and wellbeing. Talking of health and wellbeing, tomorrow we will be learning another technique that is not only great for lucid dreaming, but also great for our bodies and brains too, the deep relaxation of hypnagogic mindfulness. Enjoy your dreams. See you tomorrow.

LESSON 12 – Meeting the Gatekeeper of the Hypnagogic State
--------------------
<v ->Yesterday, we looked at all the different stages of sleep.</v> Today, we'll be focusing on just one, the hypnagogic state. A state of mind so trippy and hallucinatory that it has been revered for thousands of years as the gatekeeper of the unconscious. The hypnagogic state is the doorway into shamanic journeying, hypnotic trance, yoga nidra, and of course, lucid dreaming. So, let's learn how it works and crucially how to access it. As we discussed earlier, the hypnagogic state is the transitional state of mind that lies between wakefulness and sleep. It's the dozy in-between state often characterized by hypnagogic imagery, the visual or often conceptual displays that flash and fade before our mind's eye as we drift off to sleep. These hypnagogic images are made up of the memories of the day, mental preoccupations and for some people, a whole load of crazy shapes, colors and faces. I imagine these eccentric displays of the mind as a bit like the flashes of color that you see during the final moments of a sunset. And just like those final moments, they offer us a rare glimpse into our own inner light. We're going to learn something called Hypnagogic mindfulness. Mindfulness meditation can be defined as knowing what's happening as it's happening. So, hypnagogic mindfulness techniques are about knowing what is happening as it's happening while we're dozing off to sleep. There are two main benefits of this technique. One, is that it teaches us to be able to stay in the hypnagogic consciously for extended periods of time. As you've seen already with the dream recall technique, and as you'll see later in the quest, so many lucid dreaming techniques require that you have the ability to rest consciously in the hypnagogic state. For long enough to do your 21 affirmations or to set your intention to have a lucid dream. The second is that it's a really good way to learn how to fall asleep because every time you enter the hypnagogic intentionally, but then pull back before you fall into sleep, you strengthen the neural pathway that allows you to find the gateway into sleep. Once you become familiar with that gateway, the possibility of falling asleep at will begins to open up to you. We pass through the hypnagogic state every time we fall asleep, which means that we have a daily opportunity to engage it with awareness and even engage mindfully, the sleep that it leads us into. It's a state of huge potential, but how can we spend more time in it than the usual 10 or so minutes that it usually takes us to fall asleep? We must learn how to harness the power of hypnagogic mindfulness. This technique is about learning to rest on the drowsy boundary of sleep. This practice can be done at night as a precursor to sleep. So I'd like you to listen to the following audio track guided meditation as you fall asleep tonight. But, it can also be practiced in the day as an alternative to the afternoon nap. And you might find that this technique refreshes your mind even more effectively than napping. So, plump up your pillow and enjoy the hypnagogic. And now for your actions for today. Firstly, practice hypnagogic mindfulness either in the daytime or as you fall asleep tonight. Number two, keep up the 3 Ds and the dream sign manifestation technique. Number three, try the dream sign manifestation exercise again, even if you haven't already. In week three, you will very quickly see that a lot of lucid dreaming techniques are based on being able to rest consciously in the hypnagogic state without blacking out. And so the hypnagogic mindfulness technique is the cornerstone of our practice. If you black out, as soon as your head hits the pillow, there are still some techniques that will work for you. But, if you could learn to rest in the hypnagogic without blacking out, you can maximize your use of all the lucid dreaming techniques. See you tomorrow when we will learn a technique to help us decode our own dreams. Until then, sleep well.

LESSON 12 – Meditation: Hypnagogic mindfulness meditation

- This technique is about learning to rest on the drowsy boundary of sleep. This practice can be done at night as a precursor to sleep, or it can be done during the day as an alternative to an afternoon nap. Lie down on your back with a pillow under your head, and one under your knees if you like. Close your eyes and adjust your body so that you are totally comfortable. There's no rush. Become aware of your breathing and then proceed to settle your mind through a light regulation of the breath. Breathing in for a count of three or four, and breathing out for a count of three or four. Breathing in for a count of three or four, and breathing out for a count of three or four. Continue at your own pace for the next couple of minutes. Now ground yourself and your body by scanning your awareness from the tips of your toes to the crown of your head, relaxing deeply as you go, I will guide you through the body scan. Bring your awareness into your feet. See if you can place your mind into your feet. Feel deeply into each one of your toes, into the sole of your foot, the heel, the arch, and the top feel deeply into your feet. With awareness comes relaxation. Allow your feet to relax deeply. And now allow your awareness to flow up through your lower legs, your ankles, calf, muscles, shins, all the way up to the level of your kneecaps. Allow your awareness to flow up through your knees, upper legs, thighs, inner thighs, buttocks, groin area. You're now aware from the tips of your toes to the level of your hips. And with awareness comes relaxation. Allow yourself to release any tension from the tips of your toes to the level of your hips. And now allow your awareness to spread up through your waist, naval area. Kidneys. Allow your awareness to spread up through the sides of your body, your abdominals, your lower back awareness, spreading up through the lower rib cage, middle back, lower chest. Allow your awareness to flow up still all the way up to the level of your armpits. You're now aware from the tips of your toes to the level of your armpits. And with awareness comes relaxation. Relax deeply. And now we move our attention to our hands. Feel in to each one of your fingers and thumbs into the palm of your hand, the back of your hand. Release any tension that you might be holding in your hands. Allow your awareness to spread up through your wrists, forearms, elbows through your biceps, triceps, shoulders, and shoulder blades. Allow your awareness to flow up through the front of your chest, your upper back, meeting, that point of awareness at the level of your armpits and sweeping round to the base of your neck. You are now aware from the tips of your toes to the base of your neck. And with awareness comes relaxation. Relax deeply. And now allow your awareness to continue moving up through your throat, sides of the neck, back of the neck, up into your face, cheekbones, eye sockets, mouth, nose, forehead, your ears, the back of your head, top of your head, forehead, crown of your head. You are now mindfully aware from the tips of your toes to the crown of your head. And with awareness comes relaxation. Your entire body is deeply relaxed. And now allow your awareness to zoom out so that your aware of your entire body as it lies or sits in space, allow yourself to rest in the awareness of your bodily sensations. Rest in this state for the next minute or so. And now I want you to bring your attention to the point between your eyebrows. Allow your attention to gather at this point between your eyebrows, direct any and all of your attention to this point between your eyebrows. If you like, you can imagine a ball of white light at this point between your eyebrows or perhaps just imagine a bright, full white moon. Imagine a bright white full moon at the point between your eyebrows. Allow your awareness to gather into this point between your eyebrows and now prepare to drop any regulation of the breathing, any movement of awareness around your body, and any visualization of the ball of white light. Now, I want you to rest, release your attention and rest nowhere to go, nothing to do resting. Allow yourself to slip into the deep relaxation of the hypnogogic state. Allow yourself to relax deeply into the support of the hypnogogic state. Relax deeply in the hypnogogic for the next couple of minutes. If you feel yourself slipping off into unconscious sleep, bring your awareness back to the feeling of your body, the feeling of your breath, the sounds in the room, or the sound of this track. Relax deeply into the hypnogogic, maintaining fully conscious awareness. Take a moment to ask yourself, how do I feel? What can I see? Take a moment to explore your experience of the hypnagogic state. If you feel yourself slipping into unconscious sleep, bring your awareness back to the feelings of your body, the awareness of your breath, the sounds in the room, and the sound of this track. Relax deeply into the hypnogogic, maintaining fully conscious awareness. And now, wherever you are in the hypnagogic state, bring your attention back to an awareness of your body, an awareness of your breath, and an awareness of my voice. If you are engaging this track as a precursor to sleep, feel free to drift off through the hypnogogic and into deep and restful sleep. If you are engaging this practice as a hypnagogic mindfulness practice, then now's the time to bring your awareness back into your body, stretching gently opening your eyes, and coming back to fully wakeful awareness, feeling refreshed, revitalized, and lucidly aware you are refreshed, revitalized, and lucidly aware.

LESSON 13 – Decode the Meaning of Your Dreams
--------------------
<v ->As we approach the end of our second week</v> and prepare to enter the Full-on-Lucid Dreaming Techniques of week three, you may have noticed that your dreams have started to increase in both vividness and potential meaning. Not all dreams are laid in with mystical meaning, some are just the brain working through daytime experiences and filing away old memory, but some of them absolutely hold deep psychological significance. Whatever you believe the truth is this, our dreams reveal the internal environment of our mind. So if you want to know what's going on in here, look to your dreams. I want to share with you a technique that will help you decode meaning from your dreams. Just as we have learned how to spot our dream signs to help us become lucid, we will now learn how to decode any possible messages from our dreamer. Today's practice isn't strictly a Lucid Dreaming Technique but so many people ask me for a method to help them decode their dreams that I thought I should include this one for you. Just to make sure that we have all the bases covered and that we have definitely created the best Lucid Dreaming Course that has ever been made, because we have, mike drop. When we interpret dreams consciously, we often try to replace the dream's intelligence with our own, but instead I believe we should try to listen to and hear with broad awareness, the tone of the dream, allowing any meaning to be naturally decoded. Our dreams don't conceal their meaning from us. It's just that we often don't understand the language of the dream. To understand a dream, we must offer it our attentive awareness and learn to decode its symbols which will be totally personal to each of us. This technique starts out from the point of view that everything in the dream is you. This is a Gestalt therapy approach to dreams and also the Buddhist approach too. So if I dream of Donald Trump it's not really about Donald Trump. It's about what Donald Trump represents to me, to me he has negative associations of misogyny and racism. So if I dream of him, he might represent my own misogyny and racism. But if my friend David, who's a Trump supporter and loves Donald Trump, if he has the same dream, to him Trump represents power, breaking boundaries and original thought. So you get it, right? And you also get how much of a waste of time dream dictionaries are. For example, let's say I have a dream of a cat, but I was attacked by a cat in childhood. And let's say you have a dream of a cat, but you love cats. And you love watching 'lol' cat videos before bed. For me, a cat decodes the meaning of childhood trauma and for you, a cat decodes the meaning of joy. We need to make our own dream dictionary based on our own personal dream content. That's what dream coding is going to allow us to do. Dream decoding helps us to pinpoint the emotional flavor of individual aspects of our dreams. It's working in a non-linear fashion, looking at the energetic association that we personally hold to each dream aspect rather than any black or white direct interpretations. We ask ourselves, what do I associate with this particular aspect of the dream? So if I have a dream about Waffles, the puppy dying, I would decode the dream as, my joy and innocence is dying. Or if I dream that Waffles is huge, like as big as a skyscraper, I would decode my dream as, my joy and innocence is huge, as big as a skyscraper. So you get it, right? Working by this theory, everything in the dream is you. So in one way, the dream is extremely egotistical, but by decoding it, we can learn deep insights into ourselves which will absolutely help to reduce the power that the ego has over us. August is a friend of mine from America, who I've been working with through one-on-one Skype sessions for a while now. At the end of one of our Skype sessions, he had what I call a door handle moment. This is what my therapist friend says happens at the end of a therapy session. When the client is just walking out the door, has their hand on the handle and says, "Oh, by the way this thing once happened to me as a child." A door handle moment, a moment of deep insight coming right at the end of a session. Now for August, his door handle moment with this say, "Oh by the way, there was another dream. It was totally random and it's probably not worth mentioning but," it was then that he told me the following dream. And when we decode it, you will see what a huge dream it was offering a deep insight into August's life. This is the dream that August told me. "The dreamscape looks like Antwerp and I'm wearing my yellow Rocky Marciano shirt. I see Alfonzo walking towards me and I bump right into him. But I pretend not to see him at first. Alfonzo talks excitedly and praises me. Then he shows me these huge jewels that are about 10 feet tall. And he says, we have to climb up them. Alfonzo asks if I will be okay. And I tell him, 'it's no problem. I've been doing a lot of climbing with Jesse Anderson recently', me and Alfonzo climb to the top of the first jewel and then I wake up." So it seems like a normal but quite crazy dream about August bumping into a couple of friends then climbing up jewel for some reason. But look at the meaning we can get from this dream once we apply dream decoding. When I decoded the dream with August, I asked him what he associated with each aspect of the dream. He started at the beginning and he told me Antwerp was a place he really likes. Then I asked him about Rocky Marciano, who was on his shirt. He said, Rocky made him think of power and masculinity. When I asked him about his friend Alfonzo he said, "He was very smart, well-read, he didn't like school. He had so much potential. I think he might symbolize my untapped potential." When I asked him about jewels he said, "Beauty and preciousness." When I asked him about Jesse Anderson, he said, "Jesse leads a successful, conventional life. Although he's known in his heart forever that it's just a silly game. He's a spiritual guy but he acts like he's not, he's a salmon really. He knows the way home. I guess he might symbolize my spiritual seeker. Maybe he represents my hidden spirituality." So now that we've got the decoded meaning from August, let's read through the dream again, but replace the key aspects with their decoded representations. Now, August's dream reads like this. "The dreamscape is a place I really love and I'm wearing power and masculinity. I see my untapped potential walking towards me and I bump right into it, but I pretend not to see it at first. My untapped potential talks excitedly and praises me, then shows me the beauty and preciousness, that are about 10 feet tall. It says we have to climb up beauty and preciousness. My untapped potential asks me if I'm okay with this. And I tell it, 'it's no problem. I've been doing a lot of climbing training with my hidden spirituality,' me and my untapped potential then climb to the top of beauty and preciousness." So you see how a seemingly random dream that August didn't even think was worth mentioning, was once decoded and reflected upon, revelatory for him and offered a powerful message about his current life path. So that's how dream decoding works. Now I want you to give it a try. Step one, pick a recent dream, which is not too long and not too complex to begin with. Step two, just like we did with August dream just now, decode each major character or aspect in the dream and then re-read the dream, replacing those characters or aspects with what they represent to you. Step three, take time to reflect upon the decoded dream and ask yourself, what is the dreamer trying to highlight for me here? And now Your Actions For Today. Firstly, decode one of your own dreams. Secondly, share that decoded dream with the Tribe. Thirdly, share how your second week is going with the Tribe. Let them know how many dream signs have you been able to spot so far? Have you had any flashes of lucidity yet? Let the Tribe know. And, finally, keep up the 3 Ds and the Dream Sign Manifestation technique. Don't forget to practice your Hypnagogic Mindfulness too. So we're almost at the end of our second week and you guys are smashing it. This is not easy work, but who wants easy when you can have transformative. Be sure to tune in tomorrow for our weekly quiz, our weekly pep talk. and of course everybody's favorite, our bedtime story. Until then. Sweet dreams.

LESSON 14 – Meditation: Bedtime Story: “The Dog's Tooth”

Get into bed, get comfy, and allow yourself to drift off to sleep. While I tell you a bedtime story, I want to tell you a story about an old dog's tooth. There was once an old and very devoted Buddhist woman who lived in Tibet with her only son. The son was a silt merchant who often made trips to northern India to trade his wares. Each time he went to India, his mother would plead with him to bring her back a Buddhist relic or holy object, which she could place on her shrine to help inspire her prayers. But each time he refused her request. After decades of pleading, the old woman who was now as stubborn as she was old, told her son that if she didn't get some sort of Buddhist relic or holy object, she would kill herself. The son placated his mother and promised that he would fulfill her wish. But the next time that he traveled to India, he returned to Tibet empty handed. In fact, he had been so busy with selling his silk that he had completely forgotten about his promise, and he only remembered his mother's threat. When he turned down the path that led to their house in a fit of panic, he scanned the path for ideas and saw the rotting corpse of a dog by the side of the road. In a flash of desperate inspiration, he pulled out one of the teeth from the corpse, wrapped it in a piece of his finest silk, and decided to present it to his mother as the tooth of the Buddha himself, one of the holiest Buddhist relics in all of existence. His mother met him at the door with a face that told him she was ready to keep her suicidal promise. So he swiftly presented her with the tooth and an elaborate tale of how he had come across it. The old woman was ecstatic and she rushed over to her small shrine where she carefully placed the deceased dog's tooth, still wrapped in finest silk and began fervently to offer it prayers and prostration of devotion. For hours and hours, days and days, she stayed at her shrine, locked in deep devotional prayer towards what she truly believed was the ancient tooth of Buddha himself. After a while, the son became concerned that his mother was becoming obsessed with what he knew to be nothing more than a poor ruse. So he went into check on her. What he saw amazed him, he found his mother mesmerized in deep meditative absorption, gazing at the silt wrap, which was now glowing and illuminated with rainbow colored light. By the extraordinary power of the woman's faith and devotional prayer. She had been granted the blessing of what she believed she was praying to, and soon she became fully enlightened and her body dissolved into rainbow light upon her death, fully lucid death. So just like the old dog's tooth, it doesn't matter what we believe in, just that we believe for it is the power of belief, the power of the mind, the power of human consciousness that allows us to access our innate power and divinity. So believe. Believe in yourself, believe in your dreams, believe in your ability to become lucid. And now with the energy of that story in your body and the belief in your ability to become lucid, close your eyes if they're still open. Allow yourself to release into the support of your bed And relax deeply into sleep. Allow your breathing to slow and your mind to relax deeply into sleep. Allow any tension in your body to dissolve as you exhale and relax deeply into sleep. Dream lucidly and fruitfully, relax deeply into sleep.

So I think that, you know, remind yourself of that. It's like there's no way the UK government would let me let me work with veterans if there was if there was a danger to this. The second thing is to remind yourself of something you said before, the kid thing. that lucid dreaming is a natural arising of the human mind. It's actually something we forget how to do. So from a Buddhist point of view, and the Dalai Lama said this, so this is a nice one to remember. Dalai Lama said, from a Buddhist point of view, the strange thing is not lucid dreaming. It is non -lucid dreaming. He says, you know, the capacity of the mind is cognizant awareness. So the fact that we have these hours each day where we completely black out, we start hallucinating and we believe the hallucinations to be real. That's madness. You know, non -lucid dreaming is madness. Lucid dreaming is sanity because we go, oh, what I thought to be real is actually an internally generated hallucination. So there's a burgeoning theory that actually every time you have a lucid dream, you are helping your mental health because lucid dreamers, their entire practice is based on knowing the difference between internally generated hallucination and reality. So if you're worried about going mad, Madness, or one of the definitions of psychosis, would be believing internally generated delusions or hallucinations to be real. Lucid dreaming trains the brain to know better than anybody else the difference between the waking state reality and internally generated hallucinations and delusions. So actually, this is benefiting our mental health. It in no way negates it or is dangerous for people. The other thing I'd say is for most people, it's just difficult to do it enough for it to have any damage. LESSON 15 – Reality Checks & The Weird Technique for Lucid Dreaming
--------------------
<v ->Welcome to week three.</v> Buckle up, because we are about to lift off. We open this week with one of the most powerful lucid dreaming techniques there is. Welcome to the weird world of reality checks. One of the most common entries into a lucid dream is by simply spotting a dream sign and becoming lucid. You're in the dream, you see your dead grandma you go my dead grandma, I must be dreaming and you're lucid. But sometimes even though you spotted the dream sign and assure you must be dreaming, is my dead grandma i must be dreaming. You look around at the rest of the dream and it's so realistic. You simply can't accept that you are in a dream. This is when you need something called reality checks. Dr. Stephen LaBerge and the researchers at the Lucidity Institute in California, working out of Stanford university have scientifically verified that there are certain things that are virtually impossible for the human mind to replicate consistently within the pre-lucid dream state. Remember that's a state where you're in the dream. You spotted a dream sign and you're asking yourself, could I be dreaming? And so these things can be used to confirm reliably whether or no you're in a dream. There are loads of different reality checks but I'll take you through three of my favorites. I know these are going to sound weird but when you first hear it, but bear with me. Number one. Looking at your outstretched hand twice in quick succession without it changing in some way. Number two. Reading text coherently twice without it changing in some way. Using digital or electrical devices without them changing, glitching or malfunctioning in some way. Okay. But how can these things be used to check to see if we're dreaming or not? It's like this during a dream the brain is working flat out to maintain the projection of our elaborately detailed dream scape in real time. And although it's amazingly good at this once pre-lucid it often struggles to replicate the detail of an intricate image, such as a piece of text or an outstretched hand twice in quick succession. So if we try to make it engage in such replication it provides a close but imperfect rendering. It's the acknowledgement of this imperfect rendering that makes us lucidly aware. So let's break it down. If you think you might be dreaming but you're not 100% sure. Look at your outstretched hand within the dream then quickly look away and look back again. Alternatively watch your hand as you flip it over and flip it back again. Or you can look at your hand, make a fist and then bring it back to normal. Either way you're asking the brain to replicate the same image twice. That's how it works. Your brain will usually struggle to reproduce an identical projection of your hand. Essentially, the dreaming brain tries its best to reproduce the image but it doesn't quite have the processing speed to do so perfectly. The variations of multiple but the result is singular and it's about expectation. You have to really expect that the hand's going to change. And of course in a dream expectation creates reality. I know this hand checking thing can sometimes be a bit hard to imagine but once you first see your hand change in a dream, it's an amazing experience. And I get a lot of emails written at four o'clock in the morning from people saying, "Oh I read your book about the thing with the hand changing. I thought it was bullshit, but Oh my God I just saw my hand change in a dream It's amazing". So I await your 4:00 AM email. Let's break it down even further but it's really important that we nail this. You're in a dream, something weird happens and you think I might be dreaming but I'm not 100% sure and before you fly off that cliff or you embrace that monster you'd better be 100% sure you're dreaming. So what do you do? You do a reality check. You look at your hand you flip it over and you look at it again. If you're dreaming, when you flip it back it will probably have changed in some way. The dreaming mind is really creative. It's definitely right brain dominant. So it will give a creative expression to your hand. I've seen my hand turn into a baby elephant. I've seen it grow three new fingers. The brain's creative in the dream. It's simply not good at replicating precise detail. Hands are pretty detailed. So really struggles to replicate them to order. In fact, it's not just hands. If you think you might be dreaming you could look at any detailed pattern look away and look back at the detail pattern and it would change in some way. The shirt I'm wearing for example, if you think you might be dreaming now look at my shirt, look away and look back. If you're dreaming the shirt will probably glitch or change in some way. The same theory applies to reading text and the use of digital equipment. What is text, but a detailed pattern that we decode into meaning. And digital equipment look at the screen of your iPhone. It's way too detailed for the brains replicate so it kind of glitches. The same goes for digital watches. In fact often if you see someone wearing an old school Casio digital watch, it might be a sign they're lucid dreamer. Lucid dreamers often use these watches to do reality checks during the day something we'll come to in a bit. Remember none of these reality checks are foolproof. None of them work 100% of the time. Reading text twice in a row has been shown to be the most effective. That is effective 95% of the time the hand reality check however is only effective 90% of the time. So that means there's a crucial 10% where you'll be in a dream full of dream signs, a blue dragon, Kanye West walking my puppy Waffles and you'll be doing reality checks but the hand won't be changing. That's when you need to fall back on the 10% of your broad mindful awareness and go okay my hand's not changing, but how do I explain the blue dragon and Kanye West with Charlie's puppy? I must be dreaming. So if you thought reality checks were weird we haven't even warmed up yet. This next technique will really stretch your imagination. This technique is called the weird technique. It's called the weird technique because you do it anytime you experience something weird. And because you look weird when you do it it works like this, although opportunities for reality checks will often crop up in your dreams naturally. They usually only engaged once you spot a dream sign and you need to confirm whether you're dreaming or not. There is a way however that you can actively hasten this process. How? By doing reality checks in the daytime. Doing reality checks in the daytime forms the basis of the weird technique. A deceptively simple method through which I have the majority of my lucid dreams. Here's how to do it. As you go about your daily life fully awake whenever something weird happens or dreamlike or synchronistic, or you experienced déjà vu or something unexpected happens, you don't ignore it. You go. Oh, could I be dreaming? And then you answer that question by doing a reality check. By doing reality checks during the daytime, whenever something weird happens this new habit will soon reappear in your dreams. But when you check the hand in the dream it'll change and you'll become lucid. So let's say right now as I'm filming this quest, something weird happens. Like I hear a police siren or something rather than ignoring it I'm going to acknowledge that and go Oh, that's weird. I didn't expect to hear a police siren. Could I be dreaming? Well, how would I tell? I would look at my hand. I'd look away. I'd look back again. Now, of course I'm not psychotic. I know I'm not dreaming right now but we often dream about what we do in the daytime. So if I can spend enough of my daytime experience going could this be a dream? could I be dreaming? could I be dreaming? Eventually I will dream about doing that but in the dream the hand will change and I will become lucid. Think of it like this. If you spend your whole day packing boxes what do you dream about that night? Packing boxes. In fact last night, I dreamt about filming the quest because the day before, what did I spend my whole day doing? Filming this quest. So if you spend your whole day asking yourself am I dreaming? Am I dreaming? Am I dreaming? And each time doing a reality check. You're very likely to dream about doing that at night. And when you dream about it, you can become lucid. So here's the rub. You need to be doing at least 10 reality checks during the day for them to start coming into your dreams. The thing with reality checks and the weird technique is that sometimes when we hear about it, we get so excited. We forget to do the technique properly. If during the day when something weird happens you go Oh, that's weird. Oh. That's not going to lead to lucid dreams. All it's going to lead to is you dreaming about your hand being in your face the whole night. So there is a three step process for doing the weird technique properly. Number one. The weird thing happens. There's a synchronicity. Something strange happens. Something falls from the sky. You see someone wearing fancy dress in the middle of the street. You think that's weird. Step two. You ask yourself the question. Am I dreaming? And you've got to really consider that question. Really suspend disbelief for a moment and ask yourself could I be dreaming? While I've had lucid dreams that look as realistic as this so you can tell. And then step three is to do the hand check. Look at the outstretch hand. Four fingers and a thumb. Flip it over, flip it back four fingers and a thumb. If there's any change in detail, you need to be aware of it. If it's the first time you've heard about reality checks and the weird technique, okay? Maybe just a couple of checks in the day and it'll start coming into your dreams. But over time you need to build them up. You need to make this a new thing that you do. This is like the secret handshake of the lucid dreamer. Every time something weird happens, you don't ignore it. You go ah, could I be dreaming? The weird technique is a great one for those of you who blackout as soon as your head hits the pillow. Because it's a daytime technique that doesn't require any hypnagogic awareness or waking up at certain times as some of the other lucid dreaming techniques do. In fact, you can get lucid from this technique alone tonight. But it requires something from this moment until you got to sleep tonight you need to be 100% aware and every time something strange, unexpected or dreamlike happens you don't ignore it. You go, Oh, that's weird. And then you do a reality check. If you can stay switched on between now and when you go to sleep tonight and rack up at least 10 reality checks before you black out. There is a very high chance that you have a lucid dream tonight. My Buddhist teacher really loves this technique because he says every time you do a reality check in the day it's like a mindfulness bell. Bong. Present state awareness. Am I awake? Am I asleep? Bong. Present state awareness. Am I asleep? Am I awake? He believes. That's the reason that leads the lucid dreams not to do with the brain processes. He says, "if you get people to step into mindful awareness enough during the day and realize that actually sometimes when we think we're awake, we're sleepwalking through life. Eventually that will permeate our dreams. And that's what makes us lose it". For those of you who've seen the Hollywood movie inception this whole reality check thing might be ringing some bells. In that movie, the lead character has so many lucid dreams that sometimes when he wakes up in the morning he can't tell, am I still in a lucid dream or am I awake? So he uses his totem to tell. He has a spinning top. He spins the spinning top. And if it falls over, that means as gravity. So he must be in the waking state. If it continues spinning, that means there's no gravity. So he's still dreaming. He uses his totem to tell whether or not he's dreaming. This is your totem. From now on if ever you want to know am I dreaming or not, look at your hand twice in a row. If you want to extend it, you can do a finger pull. Now I can be pulling my finger. All I like in the waking state, it is not going to extend but in the pre-lucid dream state if I pull my finger, it goes whoop. And I go okay. I'm clearly dreaming. So this is like a grounding exercise too. It lets you know am I awake? Am I asleep? It's a really powerful exercise. And it's one which you can use to get lucid tonight. And now here are your actions for today. Aim to do 10 weird technique reality checks by the time you fall asleep tonight. And then share that experience with the tribe. How was it? How many weird things were you aware of? Did you notice that life started presenting you with more weirdness once you on the lookout for it? And secondly, keep up the three D's dream recall, dream diaries and checking your dream signs. Also don't forget the practice, the dream sign manifestation exercise we learned last week too. The weird technique really is the golden ticket to lucidity for many people. It is how I have the majority of my lucid dreams. So I know how well it works. See you tomorrow. When we find out what to do when reality checks don't work we put a cigar between our teeth. We remind ourselves of the 1970's and we learn how to get lucid with Lieutenant Columbo.
